  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f64ce465-9dde-41bd-8a7b-40f85716329a'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3718074204323940789">"I am confiding this manuscript to space, not with the intention of saving myself, but to help, perhaps, to avert the appalling scourge that is menacing the human race. Lord have pity on us!"<br/><br/>With these words, Pierre Boulle hurtles the reader onto the Planet of the Apes. In this simian world, civilization is turned upside down: apes are men and men are apes; apes rule and m</span>
  <span id="freeText3718074204323940789" style="display:none">"I am confiding this manuscript to space, not with the intention of saving myself, but to help, perhaps, to avert the appalling scourge that is menacing the human race. Lord have pity on us!"<br /><br />With these words, Pierre Boulle hurtles the reader onto the Planet of the Apes. In this simian world, civilization is turned upside down: apes are men and men are apes; apes rule and men run wild; apes think, speak, produce, wear clothes, and men are speechless, naked, exhibited at fairs, used for biological research. On the planet of the apes, man, having reached to apotheosis of his genius, has become inert.<br /><br />To this planet come a journalist and a scientist. The scientist is put into a zoo, the journalist into a laboratory. Only the journalist retains the spiritual strength and creative intelligence to try to save himself, to fight the appalling scourge, to remain a man.<br /><br />Out of this situation, Pierre Boulle has woven a tale as harrowing, bizarre, and meaningful as any in the brilliant roster of this master storyteller. With his cutomary wit, irony, and disciplined intellect and style, the author of <i>The Bridge Over the River Kwai</i> tells a swiftly moving story dealing with man's conflicts, and takes the reader into a suspenseful and strangely fascinating orbit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3718074204323940789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_948511108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/948511108" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/948511108?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer948511108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16584455164319370578">I think Pierre Boulle’s novel Planet of the Apes is a social fantasy, an allegory for revealing our civilization as blindly mimicking our past, as “aping” the good and bad of what has come before. It is a statement against complacency, a warning that history will repeat itself if we are not eternally vigilant. The novel may also be read as a cautionary illustration of our relationship with our environment and the animals with which we share the Earth.<br/><br/>Or it’s a fun science fiction book about chim</span>
  <span id="freeText16584455164319370578" style="display:none">I think Pierre Boulle’s novel Planet of the Apes is a social fantasy, an allegory for revealing our civilization as blindly mimicking our past, as “aping” the good and bad of what has come before. It is a statement against complacency, a warning that history will repeat itself if we are not eternally vigilant. The novel may also be read as a cautionary illustration of our relationship with our environment and the animals with which we share the Earth.<br><br>Or it’s a fun science fiction book about chimps, orangutans and gorillas ruling a planet.<br><br>Written by Pierre Boule and first published in 1963, as La Planète des singes, this bears a closer literary resemblance to Edgar Rice Burroughs or Jules Verne than to modern science fiction. Boulle himself, the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1351174.The_Bridge_Over_the_River_Kwai" title="The Bridge Over the River Kwai by Pierre Boulle" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bridge Over the River Kwai</a>, described the novel as a social fantasy. <br><br>There is a scene of racial memory that is especially noteworthy, but a fine work throughout. I can say after reading the original novel that all of the films have been loosely based upon Boulle’s literature; although the most recent series may ultimately be the closest to Boulle’s vision. I am coming to believe that the 1960s were the zenith of science fiction and this is a good example.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1172598444l/196057.jpg" width="244" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16584455164319370578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184822662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184822662" />
    <a title="Henry Avila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila"><img alt="Henry Avila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307597403p2/5431458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184822662?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Avila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Avila" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila">Henry Avila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184822662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4528900271628727882">When a film becomes so immensely popular they achieve pop culture status, such as The Planet of the Apes, (1968's version with Charlton Heston of course) and the many different reincarnations that follow, nothing can match it... including ironically the book which originated all the hubbub. Now a return to this novel and examine the quality of, not an even contest since countless hundreds of millions have viewed the motion picture, with relatively speaking a few million read the publication I'm </span>
  <span id="freeText4528900271628727882" style="display:none">When a film becomes so immensely popular they achieve pop culture status, such as The Planet of the Apes, (1968's version with Charlton Heston of course) and the many different reincarnations that follow, nothing can match it... including ironically the book which originated all the hubbub. Now a return to this novel and examine the quality of, not an even contest since countless hundreds of millions have viewed the motion picture, with relatively speaking a few million read the publication I'm guessing. A futuristic couple Jinn and Phyllis acting appropriately bored, while taking a soothing, leisurely vacation in remote , dark, endless Space still strangely enthralling in the distant year of A.D. 2500 ... <br />They quite unexpectedly arrive upon an object outside their spaceship. Curious the pair retreats the item and memories go back to the days of sailing ships on the high seas of Earth, come forth with a rush . A message in a bottle is found, imagine; the manuscript is in the ancient language of the third rock from the Sun, French ...However Jinn having been well educated there and can read the papers though, he uncovers the author's name... written by Ulysse Merou and telling of an expedition from our world to the giant star Betelgeuse, 642 light years from good old Earth, their object was to explore planets suspected of orbiting that legendary star, maybe find life. Along with journalist Merou , are botanist Professor Antellet and physician Arthur Levain, when landing on one of the four planets discovered, they surprisingly meet humanoid like mutes, harmless creatures, primitives to be honest and easily dominated by the spacemen. Soon however the Earthmen, along with the natives are ambushed by...Apes more human than humans , no exaggeration either nor dream brutal reality sets in quickly and consequences begin ...Slaughtering them these intelligent ape-like animals; the men run for their lives but are soon captured, separated from his friends Ulysse is put in a humiliating cage with enchanting Nova a female mute he has befriended. This planet of the apes looks at Merou like a lowly animal in a zoo, leaving this upside down place is the ultimate goal of Ulysse, a nice place to visit but you wouldn't want to live there. A fine satire of the silliness of our world's numerous foibles and downright if I may say the old- fashioned word evil, everything changes but all remains the same...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4528900271628727882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14594867228938140714" style="display:none">ENGLISH (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/414895.Planet_of_the_Apes" title="Planet of the Apes by Pierre Boulle" rel="nofollow noopener">Planet of the Apes</a>) / ITALIANO<br><br><blockquote>«Jinn and Phyllis were spending a wonderful holiday in space, as far away as possible from the inhabited stars»</blockquote> A couple of tourists on an interplanetary trip runs into a bottle drifting in the space. <div id="review_449771038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449771038" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/449771038?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      501 Must Read Books (Sci-Fi)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=501">501</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=with-movie">with-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449771038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7933079206779879383">French writer Pierre Boulle (1912-1994) made use of his experience as a soldier in WWII in depicting the relationship of apes and men in this 1963 book, <i>Planet of the Apes.</i> While stationed in Indochina in 1943, he was captured by Vichy France loyalists on the Mekong River and was subjected to severe hardship and forced labour. The way the loyalists treated him and his fellow Gaulle and resistance supporters inspired Boulle to write this novel.<br/><br/>This book was highly praised and was given such revie</span>
  <span id="freeText7933079206779879383" style="display:none">French writer Pierre Boulle (1912-1994) made use of his experience as a soldier in WWII in depicting the relationship of apes and men in this 1963 book, <i>Planet of the Apes.</i> While stationed in Indochina in 1943, he was captured by Vichy France loyalists on the Mekong River and was subjected to severe hardship and forced labour. The way the loyalists treated him and his fellow Gaulle and resistance supporters inspired Boulle to write this novel.<br /><br />This book was highly praised and was given such reviews as this example from England's Guardian newspaper: <i>"Classic science fiction...full of suspense and satirical intelligence."</i> I agree to this. It is a sci-fi because of the idea of having apes ruling the universe as they think that men have lesser intelligence than them. The Ape planet, called <i>Soror</i> (Latin for sister), revolves around the red Sun called <i>Betelguese</i> (that is real). Then the ape scientists in the said planet conduct Pavlov-like experiments to their captured human beings and one of the three was <b>Ulysse,</b> the author of the journal found floating in the space as narrated in the frame story. His companion, the genius scientist from Earth, <b>Professor Antell</b> turns crazy while his fellow crew, physicist <b>Arthur Levaine</b> is killed during the landing of their spaceship. <br /><br />For me, its main theme is an reminder of the things we take for granted or better yet, the people who we take for granted. Sometimes, we think that they are <u>lesser</u> than us: in stature, job title, wealth, skin color, etc. But in reality, we don't realize that they can be <u>more</u> than us. It's just that we are too focused on ourselves that we don't see what they have that we lack. <br /><br />For example as a reader, we think that we all pick and read the better books and we look down on people who read <i>other</i> books not realizing that those could be better than what we are reading.<br /><br />This book is a sci-fi and I know some people look down on sci-fi readers. Not true, figment of imagination, will never happen, yadda, yadda. But hey, how about this main theme that I deduced from this book?</span>
  <a data-text-id="7933079206779879383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3332234089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3332234089" />
    <a title="Brett C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1986675-brett-c"><img alt="Brett C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544197549p2/1986675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3332234089?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brett C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brett C" href="/user/show/1986675-brett-c">Brett C</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer6679904078375414126">I enjoyed this story. I can say both the book and the movie are great in their own way.   <span id="freeText6679904078375414126" style="display:none">I enjoyed this story. I can say both the book and the movie are great in their own way. The movie was science fiction but the book seemed more socially-based lo-fi science fiction. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589504948i/29477807._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The book goes way more in depth about the planet our narrator and his crew have landed on. Through the narrator we discover much more about the ape planet than the movie gives. The interaction between the primitive man, chimpanzees, gorillas, and orangutans follows the movie yet the author does a great job of telling the tale. <br><br>On the planet exists social constructs and norms, a Simian language, art and science, zoos, lobotomy experiments, and more. Lastly, we discover how the shift occurred and monkeys came to rule the world. <br><br>Pierre Boulle has a unique way of telling a story full of detail yet is entertaining and creative. Overall I enjoyed this book and would recommend it to anyone who likes any movies from the franchise. Thanks!</span>

<div id="review_3468858985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3468858985" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3468858985?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3468858985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer395696328050028295">This is a book that deserves to stand the test of time. I think it's as valid now as it was back in the fifties.<br/><br/>Let's ignore the movies for just a moment. They're important in their own right for capturing a cultural zeitgeist and for showing us all how damning cultural bias can be. One can make the argument that the Planet of the Apes movies underscored the 60's, put it all in sharp relief. <br/><br/>But I'm going to talk about the book -- about why the book needs to be read now.<br/><br/>Cultural bias is everywhe</span>
  <span id="freeText395696328050028295" style="display:none">This is a book that deserves to stand the test of time. I think it's as valid now as it was back in the fifties.<br /><br />Let's ignore the movies for just a moment. They're important in their own right for capturing a cultural zeitgeist and for showing us all how damning cultural bias can be. One can make the argument that the Planet of the Apes movies underscored the 60's, put it all in sharp relief. <br /><br />But I'm going to talk about the book -- about why the book needs to be read now.<br /><br />Cultural bias is everywhere. All around us. It's in the very air we breathe. In general, we don't see it.<br /><br />Our assumptions make us prisoners. <br /><br />The apes are the epitome of Western Thought. Casually racist in everything they do, they rationalize everyone OTHER than themselves into a kind of slavery. Whether it's about cultural superiority, scientific superiority, military superiority, or ANY reason to make themselves appear more important than the OTHER, they take it.<br /><br />Because what would happen otherwise?<br /><br />Rhetoric would fall apart, giving way to a careful observation of the real circumstances. <br /><br />People are being kept in cages. They're experimented upon. They are left in atrocious conditions and made to fight for scraps to survive. The purpose is to turn them into animals FIRST in order to prove the original assumption that they are animals.<br /><br />If this isn't classic racism, I don't know what is. Every argument they make must revolve around the basic assumption that THEY are better than US. If the argument doesn't fit, it is thrown out.<br /><br />Only OVERWHELMING evidence to the contrary can lift a single human out of this bondage, and but the great emancipation only works for this single human.<br /><br />The pervasive racism persists.<br /><br />Classic cultural bias.<br /><br />We are fully immersed in it. We feel the hopelessness underlying their bulwarks of rationalizations. We are made small, helpless, even as we retain our dignity in all the tiniest of ways. And ultimately, we lose. <br /><br /><br /><br />It takes a whole society to change a whole society. </span>
  <a data-text-id="395696328050028295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_65840383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65840383" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65840383?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451160164" href="/book/show/1650178.Planet_of_the_Apes">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Becky by: </span>
      Kandice Zelaskowski
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65840383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7001599744708167051">Caution: Vague Spoilers Ahead<br/><br/>I don't really think that I can do this book justice in my review. I thought that it was brilliant. I know that I have seen the movie long ago, and remember the big reveal at the end and Charlton yelling about damning everyone all to hell, but I don't remember much more than that. I'll have to watch the movie again.<br/><br/>I really loved the subtle cautionary tale running throughout the story. Maybe it's just my feminist liberal bleeding heart whispering to me, but I feel th</span>
  <span id="freeText7001599744708167051" style="display:none">Caution: Vague Spoilers Ahead<br /><br />I don't really think that I can do this book justice in my review. I thought that it was brilliant. I know that I have seen the movie long ago, and remember the big reveal at the end and Charlton yelling about damning everyone all to hell, but I don't remember much more than that. I'll have to watch the movie again.<br /><br />I really loved the subtle cautionary tale running throughout the story. Maybe it's just my feminist liberal bleeding heart whispering to me, but I feel that Boulle just plain hated live-animal experiments and was determined to show people that the tables could be turned one day. Easily. But more than that, the book cautions us not to be complacent and lazy about our place in life and in the food chain and to keep striving and learning and bettering ourselves, but NOT at the cost of other life-forms. We're on top now, but only time will tell if we stay there. <br /><br />And do we actually deserve to be? We, the "Lords of Creation," seem to think that we can do anything and everything we want to do. We're so filled with pride that we never think that OUR civilization could fall. Those kind of things are for history books, not real life. Yet we consume resources like they're going out of style, and pollute the earth like we have a spare, and just generally act like there's a "Reset" button somewhere that we can just press when we've reached the point of no return. Why shouldn't another species give running things a try? If they can do it better... <br /><br />But that's the thing. They imitate us, so WOULD they do it better? At one point in the story, when Merou was being shown the experiments, I thought to myself, <i>"They are proud of the fact that they are keeping the "animals" down... Taking any vestiges of humanity or rational thought away as soon as it is displayed in order to protect themselves. They are so fearful of the possibility of human uprising that they commit atrocities to prevent them."</i> And then I thought to myself, <i>"Oh, snap! So do we."</i> We can justify anything. And so can Apes, who apparently learned from the best. In examining the Apes, we're looking at ourselves. Can we really pass judgment?<br /><br />But, I was happy to see that the three "races" of Apes could cohabitate and cooperate in peace, which is more than we've accomplished so far. Our differences divide us, but the Apes recognize and relish their differences and use them well. But Apes still seem to rival Man in the fear department: the unknown is scary, so just destroy it and move on.<br /><br />I do have to say that I was kind of annoyed with Merou's assumption that life forms in a far, far away galaxy would automatically be human to be intelligent. It just goes to show that our pride will be our downfall. But it reminded me of a quote from another science-fiction book that I enjoyed, Solaris by Stanislaw Lem (which you should remember if you keep up with my reviews):<br /><br /><blockquote>"...We take off into the cosmos, ready for anything: for solitude, for hardship, for exhaustion, death. Modesty forbids us to say so, but there are times when we think pretty well of ourselves. And yet, if we examine it more closely, our enthusiasm turns out to be all sham. We don't want to conquer the cosmos, we simply want to extend the boundaries of Earth to the frontiers of the cosmos. For us, such and such a planet is as arid as the Sahara, another as frozen as the North Pole, yet another as lush as the Amazon basin. We are humanitarian and chivalrous; we don't want to enslave other races, we simply want to bequeath them our values and take over their heritage in exchange. We think of ourselves as the Knights of the Holy Contact. This is another lie. We are only seeking Man. We have no need of other worlds. We need mirrors. We don't know what to do with other worlds. [...:] We arrive here as we are in reality, and when the page is turned and that reality is revealed to us--that part of our reality which we would prefer to pass over in silence--then we don't like it anymore." </blockquote><br /><br />Oh, it's so apt. We inherently assume that anyone of any worth or intelligence will be just like us. Even the "Little Green Men" type aliens that pop up in the Weekly World News magazines are still modeled after humans, and hell, they are nicknamed "men"! I just hope that one day we'll be able to see the bigger picture.<br /><br />I do want to mention two things that I wish were clarified a little more in the book. I'd been told that the twist in the book was different than the twist in the movie. I had had a theory that somehow during the journey from Earth, something got mixed up and the planet they landed on WAS Earth, only far in the future. Since it seems that was not correct, I'm confused as to how two planets so distant actually would be so very similar. The two main races (Apes and humans) are the same genetically (or so it seems as Merou was able to successfully mate with an "alien" human), and there are several other animals that are similar. Not to mention the society and transportation etc. It just seems so unlikely that Soror would be so similar to Earth without knowing of its existence. <br /><br />And speaking of which, that brings me to the second thing. Merou named the planet Soror prior to meeting any sentient beings. Didn't they have their own name for the planet? I cannot believe that throughout ANY of the discussions they had regarding the origins of their species, or space travel, or anything, that they did not once say, "Oh, and by the way, we call our planet Apex." (Haha, get it?) But really, that point bothered me in the story. <br /><br />Anyway, Aside from those two points, I thought that this was a really great book. I hope that everyone gets a chance to read it one day. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7001599744708167051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_613631356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613631356" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/613631356?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780814900642" href="/book/show/263384.Planet_of_the_Apes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613631356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8762239860853240477"><b>"Almost all the great discoveries," she stated vehemently, "have been made by chimpanzees."</b><br/><br/>Experimentation is needed for all great discoveries, and what would a chimpanzee use as a lab animal? Why, a human, of course! Oh, those damn dirty apes!<br/><br/>Despite Charleton Heston's scenery-chewing, I've always loved <i>Planet of the Apes</i>, the movie. <br/>The book? Well, it gets off to an awkward start. <br/><br/>The writing is clunky, and the plot, so improbable - <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[A couple is "sailing" in space when they come </span></span>
  <span id="freeText8762239860853240477" style="display:none"><b>"Almost all the great discoveries," she stated vehemently, "have been made by chimpanzees."</b><br /><br />Experimentation is needed for all great discoveries, and what would a chimpanzee use as a lab animal? Why, a human, of course! Oh, those damn dirty apes!<br /><br />Despite Charleton Heston's scenery-chewing, I've always loved <i>Planet of the Apes</i>, the movie. <br />The book? Well, it gets off to an awkward start. <br /><br />The writing is clunky, and the plot, so improbable - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A couple is "sailing" in space when they come upon a message in a bottle. Seriously. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - I actually thought about trotting this right back to the library, but I kept saying to myself, "This is the same guy who wrote <i>Bridge Over the River Kwai</i>...how bad can it be?"<br /><br />Not bad at all, it turns out, though I'm still not sure first-person was the way to go. <br /><br />The movie was mostly faithful to the book. <br /><br />The main character is a Frenchman named Ulysse. The apes do not speak the same language, which makes for some interesting communication problems. There is also some friction between the chimps, the orangutans and the gorillas, with each group believing theirs is the superior collection of beings. <br /><br />Dr. Zaius <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4n8BPv43vhE">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4n8BPv...</a> is much the same in the book as in the movie, part orangutan/ part jackass.<br /><br />And I was quite pleased that one of my favorite bits in the film was taken directly from the book - the sweet, somewhat flirty relationship between Zira and her too-ugly-to-kiss human captive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8762239860853240477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1754968038?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Mathews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Mathews" href="/user/show/22063432-tom-mathews">Tom Mathews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22063432-tom-mathews?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22063432-tom-mathews?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22063432-tom-mathews?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22063432-tom-mathews?shelf=video-adaptation">video-adaptation</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1754968038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15818531132191228500">Originally written in 1963 by the same author who brought us <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1351174.The_Bridge_Over_the_River_Kwai' title='The Bridge Over the River Kwai by Pierre Boulle' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bridge Over the River Kwai</a>, this book will most likely be remembered for the many movies that were based on it's premise of a world where the roles of apes and men are reversed. Originally written in French, the main character in the novel is Ulysse Mérou: A journalist who took part in the space expedition that lands on Soror, a planet orbiting the star Betelgeuse. There is some argument as to whether the book can be considered sci</span>
  <span id="freeText15818531132191228500" style="display:none">Originally written in 1963 by the same author who brought us <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1351174.The_Bridge_Over_the_River_Kwai" title="The Bridge Over the River Kwai by Pierre Boulle" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bridge Over the River Kwai</a>, this book will most likely be remembered for the many movies that were based on it's premise of a world where the roles of apes and men are reversed. Originally written in French, the main character in the novel is Ulysse Mérou: A journalist who took part in the space expedition that lands on Soror, a planet orbiting the star Betelgeuse. There is some argument as to whether the book can be considered science fiction or if it's a work of satire in the vein of Gulliver's Travel. Personally,I tend to see most science fiction as a study of society so I'm not going to say this isn't it. <br /><br />Bottom line: PotA is an entertaining read but not extremely imaginative. I listened to the audio version recorded by Greg Wise in 2012 and was surprised to find that in many cases the word <b>ape</b> in the print version was changed to <b>monkey</b> in the audio recording. As one who knows that apes and monkeys come from distinct simian families, I felt the change made no sense and found it extremely irritating. <br /><br />Thanks to the Goodreads Time Travel reading group for choosing this book and giving me the opportunity to read and discuss it with others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15818531132191228500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_11593858" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11593858" />
    <a title="Kirk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/667059-kirk"><img alt="Kirk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442453577p2/667059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11593858?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirk" href="/user/show/667059-kirk">Kirk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451160164" href="/book/show/1650178.Planet_of_the_Apes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/667059-kirk?shelf=sentimental-faves">sentimental-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11593858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer514419276388925286">So in fourth grade we had an assignment to write our favorite author. Being a dork, I went for Pierre Boulle because he had written the only book I knew of that let you put on a gorilla mask and run around like you'd taken over the world. Imagine my surprise when one day a letter from Paris arrived in the mail from none other than the very tolerant Mr. Boulle (then about sixty), who answered such probing questions as "Why are Jinn and Phyllis not in the movie?" (There's an opening narrative fram</span>
  <span id="freeText514419276388925286" style="display:none">So in fourth grade we had an assignment to write our favorite author. Being a dork, I went for Pierre Boulle because he had written the only book I knew of that let you put on a gorilla mask and run around like you'd taken over the world. Imagine my surprise when one day a letter from Paris arrived in the mail from none other than the very tolerant Mr. Boulle (then about sixty), who answered such probing questions as "Why are Jinn and Phyllis not in the movie?" (There's an opening narrative frame featuring two swinging astronauts having a holiday in space....) I still have the letter Mr. B sent me (yes, it's framed, but no, it's not hanging on a wall). Unfortunately, I don't have the two or three subsequent letters where he even more tolerantly entertained my endless ideas for even more Planet of the Ape-sequels. And Lord knows I fear the thought that somewhere in some French library a scholar is poring over scratchy Michigan penmanship wondering what the hell the author of THE BRIDGE OVER THE RIVER KWAI was doing wasting his time with fan letters from nine-year olds. Please, God, don't letter there ever be a scholarly edition of Mr. B's correspondence.<br /><br />Anyway, the other day AMC ran the entire PoftheA marathon, but I was busy (reading!), so I didn't watch. Still, it reminded me that it'd been more than 30 years since I read this, so I went and dug it out. For Roddy McDowell fans, be prepared: this is not your father's Charleton Heston. Yes, there's Drs. Cornelius and Zira, and the stratified ape society, but there's no "get your stinking paws off of me, you damned dirty ape"---and no statue of liberty surprise ending (Pierre Boulle was French, remember). This is a fast-paced, literate satire that tweaks human vanity, science, classism, and Peter Tork---well, ok there's no Peter Tork. But he's about the only thing in 50s/60s society that doesn't get a ribbing. Fun stuff, inevitably tainted by boyhood nostalgia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="514419276388925286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_199740719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/199740719?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=better-as-a-movie">better-as-a-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199740719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17703756896475291255">The original Planet of the Apes novel is a seriously clunky story. It is bookended by a kooky couple in space who find a message in a bottle <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[psst ... they turn out to be Chimps <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Ulysse Mérou stands in as a more pedantic Taylor who gets to knock up Nova before they with their child, and the Ape society is more developed, which makes it less effective in creating that Planet of the Apes vibe.<br/><br/>If it weren't for the movie with its killer Rod Serling script and the aweso</span>
  <span id="freeText17703756896475291255" style="display:none">The original Planet of the Apes novel is a seriously clunky story. It is bookended by a kooky couple in space who find a message in a bottle <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[psst ... they turn out to be Chimps <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Ulysse Mérou stands in as a more pedantic Taylor who gets to knock up Nova before they with their child, and the Ape society is more developed, which makes it less effective in creating that Planet of the Apes vibe.<br /><br />If it weren't for the movie with its killer Rod Serling script and the awesomeness of Charlton Heston (when he was the coolest Sci-Fi actor around), and all the sequels and TV shows and reboots that have followed, the original <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/414895.Planet_of_the_Apes" title="Planet of the Apes by Pierre Boulle" rel="nofollow noopener">Planet of the Apes</a> novel wouldn't deserve much in terms of goodreads stars. But all those movies did follow <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5765.Pierre_Boulle" title="Pierre Boulle" rel="nofollow noopener">Pierre Boulle</a>'s book, and my unquenchable nostalgia for all things Ape will always elevate this in my estimation. That's just the kind of geek I am.<br /><br />My Planet of the Apes loving credentials:<br /><br />• own the box set of the original film series.<br />• own Reality Bites just because of Ben Stiller's Planet of the Apes figures.<br />• owned Planet of the Apes toys as a kid.<br />• actively hunt down movie-tie-ins and any other Planet of the Apes books I can find.<br />• have crappy old VHS tapes with about half of the TV episodes on them.<br />• quote Charlton Heston and Roddy McDowell on a regular basis, seamlessly.<br />• played Planet of the Apes with my friend Dwayne instead of playing at Soldiers, and now I get to do it with my son and daughter.<br />• I teach the film version of Planet of the Apes regularly, and I've even mixed it up a bit with Conquest of the Planet of the Apes.<br />• tried to convince Erika to name Milos, Taylor Cornelius<br />• AND I named my dog Zira.<br /><br />I'm probably forgetting some stuff, but that's a good list to start. I may add to my geek credentials as I remember them.<br /><br />And check out the geek credentials on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1019174-terence" rel="nofollow noopener">Terence</a> if you get a chance. Just look at his icon for the love of Caesar!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17703756896475291255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_26514561" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26514561" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1177534-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593697601p2/1177534.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26514561?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1177534-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=obscure-references-book-group">obscure-references-book-group</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26514561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12226401050735288583">“Planet of the Apes” is one of those books that’s hard to approach without bringing along the baggage of the original 60s film adaptation or the less-than-successful remake a few years ago. The original film is such a part of our pop-culture concsiousness that it’s almost impossible to separate it from what we have here.<br/><br/>This is one of those books that is what it is–no more, no less. <br/><br/>I could spend several paragraphs detailing the differences between the movie and the book, but that would be kind </span>
  <span id="freeText12226401050735288583" style="display:none">“Planet of the Apes” is one of those books that’s hard to approach without bringing along the baggage of the original 60s film adaptation or the less-than-successful remake a few years ago. The original film is such a part of our pop-culture concsiousness that it’s almost impossible to separate it from what we have here.<br /><br />This is one of those books that is what it is–no more, no less. <br /><br />I could spend several paragraphs detailing the differences between the movie and the book, but that would be kind of pointless and wouldn’t tell you much about the book as a whole. That said, Boulle’s original novel is a social satire, as advertises and it’s one of what I’d classify as a fairly light, “bubble-gum” sci-fi read. It has just enough in there to make you think while reading it, but it’s not going to stay with you long after you’ve finished the final pages. <br /><br />The thing is that not a lot of the characters have much depth. They’re all in here to be part of the satire of modern life and humanity’s relationship with each other and animals. For a satire that wants to point out how drawing distinctions based on external apperances isn’t a great thing, you’d think it would have a bit more depth to the characters. Add to that that the central narrator has a tendency to become a bit pompous in his relation of events and you’ve got a story that works, quite frankly, better as a movie than it does as a novel. I’d even go so far as to say that without the series of movies, this is one novel that would have faded in memory long ago, remembered by some who read it for a few of the twists in the final pages but not much more.<br /><br />It’s not to say I hated this novel. But it’s not to say I loved it or found it nearly as compelling as some of the mid-range works by Issac Asimov or Orson Scott Card. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12226401050735288583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5104780929793697467">There is something so bizarrely enticing about throwing your conceptions of the world utterly and completely upside down. In so doing, you see yourself and the world in a whole new way, one which you might not like. This is what Planet of the Apes does so well. This is a great read. Compared to the film, I found it quite a bit more introspective, lacking much of the action, violence and campy drama.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer7277209471003388397">I read this years ago....about the time of the Heston film. I liked the opening and the little twist he (tried to) give it but all in all the book wasn't all that great I thought.<br/><br/>By the way there are differences in the book and the movie, a surprise, right?<br/><br/>I don't know what it is/was that left me cold on this one. I'd rate it 1.5 if could, but I can't and to rate it actually a 1 would rank it with some books I've found really detestable, so 2 even though I really am not that found of the book. I</span>
  <span id="freeText7277209471003388397" style="display:none">I read this years ago....about the time of the Heston film. I liked the opening and the little twist he (tried to) give it but all in all the book wasn't all that great I thought.<br /><br />By the way there are differences in the book and the movie, a surprise, right?<br /><br />I don't know what it is/was that left me cold on this one. I'd rate it 1.5 if could, but I can't and to rate it actually a 1 would rank it with some books I've found really detestable, so 2 even though I really am not that found of the book. In fact I suppose you could say overall, I disliked it. The idea was pretty good, an interesting concept. The set up wasn't bad, but the overall feel of the book and its predictability were just sad. (Actually, in more ways than one.) <br /><br />So, not as bad as some 1 stars I've read, but not so great either. Maybe you'll like more, to each their own as they say, but not for me.<br /><br />As to predictability, I mentioned the "twist" he tried for, but (if you've read it yet) were you really surprised?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5496569516725965803">The Planet of the Apes movie is probably my favourite of all time. It was very interesting to read the original source material and see the differences. The biggest difference is the ending, although without giving any spoilers, it does match up with later movies in the series.<br/><br/>The writing is excellent. The book focusses more on the science-y stuff such as the experiments the apes are performing on the humans, how they would have evolved differently, etc. It was great food for thought. It was mis</span>
  <span id="freeText5496569516725965803" style="display:none">The Planet of the Apes movie is probably my favourite of all time. It was very interesting to read the original source material and see the differences. The biggest difference is the ending, although without giving any spoilers, it does match up with later movies in the series.<br /><br />The writing is excellent. The book focusses more on the science-y stuff such as the experiments the apes are performing on the humans, how they would have evolved differently, etc. It was great food for thought. It was missing some of the big twists and turns which made the story more theatrical for the film. I was still engrossed in the story and if you're a fan of the movie, it's definitely worth reading the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5496569516725965803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_321999738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321999738" />
    <a title="Amy Sturgis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3982049-amy-sturgis"><img alt="Amy Sturgis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442475846p2/3982049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321999738?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Sturgis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Sturgis" href="/user/show/3982049-amy-sturgis">Amy Sturgis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451160164" href="/book/show/1650178.Planet_of_the_Apes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3982049-amy-sturgis?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3982049-amy-sturgis?shelf=postapocalyptic-dystopia">postapocalyptic-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3982049-amy-sturgis?shelf=science-fiction-vintage">science-fiction-vintage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321999738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13172742152281628564">I thoroughly enjoyed this novel. I'm quite familiar with the classic film adaptation of it, but this was my first time to read the original text, and I was delighted and fascinated by the differences between the two, small and large, from the introductory framing of the story (in the novel, as a space-faring couple's discovery of a "message in a bottle" floating through space) to the "big reveal" of its great twist. <br/><br/>The dystopian elements of the tale are chilling and still quite timely. I partic</span>
  <span id="freeText13172742152281628564" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed this novel. I'm quite familiar with the classic film adaptation of it, but this was my first time to read the original text, and I was delighted and fascinated by the differences between the two, small and large, from the introductory framing of the story (in the novel, as a space-faring couple's discovery of a "message in a bottle" floating through space) to the "big reveal" of its great twist. <br /><br />The dystopian elements of the tale are chilling and still quite timely. I particularly appreciated the emphasis on the horrors of a so-called advanced species' choice to use another for scientific experimentation and the swiftness with which humans (as individuals or as a group) may devolve into brutes. The relationship between the human Ulysse and his keeper/savior/patron, the chimpanzee Zira, is particularly well drawn, as are the divisions and political posturing within the monkeys' society.<br /><br />A few small notes struck me as false -- I found the use of suddenly-tapped atavistic memory as a plot device to be rather weak, not to mention jarring -- but on the whole this hit far more often than it missed. The questions it raises about the arbitrary and often unthinking power humans exert over other creatures are lasting and important, and I appreciate how Boulle puts us, as it were, in our place.<br /><br />I'm glad I read this. It deserves its respected position in genre history. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13172742152281628564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167104259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167104259" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2906120-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435004645p2/2906120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167104259?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/2906120-vanessa">Vanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451160164" href="/book/show/1650178.Planet_of_the_Apes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2906120-vanessa?shelf=top-10-of-2012">top-10-of-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167104259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11395065168102331308">The ultimate Sci-Fi classic that started it all - I am pleased to say - totally holds up to its former glory!<br/><br/>First of all, I was shocked to find that after calling/visiting five - YES FIVE - independent bookstores in Boston, NONE of them carried this book. Really? I mean, really??! I finally had to resort to ordering it on amazon (YUCK) - a COMPLETE last resort. Anyways, I am still completely befuddled as to why this is not more widely available and read as I feel it is just as important as SF s</span>
  <span id="freeText11395065168102331308" style="display:none">The ultimate Sci-Fi classic that started it all - I am pleased to say - totally holds up to its former glory!<br /><br />First of all, I was shocked to find that after calling/visiting five - YES FIVE - independent bookstores in Boston, NONE of them carried this book. Really? I mean, really??! I finally had to resort to ordering it on amazon (YUCK) - a COMPLETE last resort. Anyways, I am still completely befuddled as to why this is not more widely available and read as I feel it is just as important as SF staples like Fahrenheit 451 and Stranger in a Strange Land. It makes no sense, whatsoever.<br /><br />But onto the good stuff! I tore through this in a matter of 2 days and loved every minute! All I knew about this story was that it took place on another planet and there was a great twist ending. So, I started with a pretty clean slate (I have never seen the movie, for instance). <br /><br />There were fantastic and extremely "discussable" (yep, I made that word up) themes in this book regarding human nature, evolution, fear of the unknown, and the morality of experimentation. It reads much like the adventure novels of Jules Verne and was very fast paced. I was totally enraptured from start to finish. Period. <br /><br />Everyone MUST read this SF classic, as it is now one of my favorites!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11395065168102331308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15575840125403460770" style="display:none">The book is similar to the film series in certain ways, but different enough to provide a new approach to the main subject. The story is told as being in a manuscript found by space travellers, so much of the story is told in narrative rather than dialogue. (It took me awhile to get used to this writing style.) The ending is very different from the film. The book seems to emphasize the theme of evolution, while the film focuses more on time travel. I liked the book, but I like the film series more. An interesting read.</span>

<div id="review_782981480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/782981480" />
    <a title="Zora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8291584-zora"><img alt="Zora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334094089p2/8291584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/782981480?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zora" href="/user/show/8291584-zora">Zora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer782981480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer745871291771520344">French feminism didn't happen any too soon, apparently. This book doesn't age well at all. It also grinds axes against hunters and animal researchers, and if you are either, you'll probably want to skip it to moderate your blood pressure. Mostly, though, the treatment of women is just not to be believed. Gah!<br/><br/>Also, there were some weird translation choices, where I could imagine what the French word had been and could think of a much better English word than the one the translator chose. "Monkeys</span>
  <span id="freeText745871291771520344" style="display:none">French feminism didn't happen any too soon, apparently. This book doesn't age well at all. It also grinds axes against hunters and animal researchers, and if you are either, you'll probably want to skip it to moderate your blood pressure. Mostly, though, the treatment of women is just not to be believed. Gah!<br /><br />Also, there were some weird translation choices, where I could imagine what the French word had been and could think of a much better English word than the one the translator chose. "Monkeys," "diving suits" and many other terms pulled me out of the story.<br /><br />I also didn't believe in the main character, a journalist who on a whim, and despite understanding time dilation effects of NAFAL travel, hops on a spaceship that will put him 800 years out of time when he returns to Earth (that's not how it ends up, of course, but that's what he thinks is going to happen.) Instead of adapting to this vastly different world, he remains bullheaded and pushy and arrogant. (And they say "ugly Americans?" This character has that act down perfectly.)<br /><br />The space mission had one of the world's great thinkers along who didn't immediately think parallel evolution was impossible? The anthropology is the worst of the sciences (the narrator thinks certain gestures are going to be universal, for instance, when they aren't even on Earth, and he keep pushing the native humans to adapt to his gestures rather than adapting to theirs), but the astronomy isn't always good, either. Chandrasekhar and Hoyle and Wilson had all published, so any half-witted astronomer, much less the great one planning the fictional mission, would have known that to travel to an unstable red giant star would have been dangerous and certainly wouldn't be visiting a star where planets still had life, if indeed they had survived the expansion of the star at all. So the author wasn't up on the stellar life cycle for his day, even, and from modern perspective, this too suffers.<br /><br />By half way through I was on the side of the intelligent apes. I wanted to stick the narrator in a cage and prod him with some sticks, too. And what the heck is the frame device about, with the ape couple on vacation (good goddess, sexism there too) reading the diary? Was that necessary?<br /><br />Can you tell I didn't like this? I didn't like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="745871291771520344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tressa " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/226335-tressa"><img alt="Tressa " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464796958p2/226335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1050176104?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tressa " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tressa " href="/user/show/226335-tressa">Tressa </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226335-tressa?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226335-tressa?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1050176104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1037961357972953464">I'm a big fan of the Planet of the Apes TV/movie franchise, but had never read the book. It is more simplistic than I thought it would be, and at times humorous when it's not supposed to be, but as it progresses the story takes a more philosophical turn and many episodes of captivity and experimentation on the humans make us ponder the morality of the way animals are treated in our culture. This is the only Apes book written by Boulle, but I am going to start collecting the other books in the se</span>
  <span id="freeText1037961357972953464" style="display:none">I'm a big fan of the Planet of the Apes TV/movie franchise, but had never read the book. It is more simplistic than I thought it would be, and at times humorous when it's not supposed to be, but as it progresses the story takes a more philosophical turn and many episodes of captivity and experimentation on the humans make us ponder the morality of the way animals are treated in our culture. This is the only Apes book written by Boulle, but I am going to start collecting the other books in the series because I think it's an interesting concept and I want to see how the story plays out. <br /><br />If readers want to read another book about animal ethics, read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2222947.Meat" title="Meat by Joseph D'Lacey" rel="nofollow noopener">Meat</a>. There's a whole lot more to ponder in this book. <br /><br /></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vCBs3kceyp0cmD4CO+bCoo8TbCmJu5IWw7acPQCDibiNnsRxcOuFOFdysJ5kivKP5kvjQzPy8r/GHaqZyQO/IQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('r4S7K0bD2F+uXOFNrH+UtHh8L+tRge96jvVk53RB4seeOhOEcTaX+uW2b9HzE6SZESSggevIj9OLXlJDvcHUXg==')})
  }

Sea-devil has appeared in the Rio de la Plata. Weird cries out at sea, slashed fishermen\'s nets, glimpses of a most queer creature astride a dolphin leave no room for doubt. The Spaniard Zurita, greed overcoming his superstition, tries to catch Sea-devil and force it to pearl-dive for him but fails. On a lonely stretch of shore, not far from Buenos Aires, Dr. Salvator lives in seclusion behind a high wall, whose steel-plated gates only open to let in his Indian patients. The Indians revere him as a God but Zurita has a hunch that the God on land and the devil in the sea have something in common. Enlisting the help of two wily Araucanian brothers he sets out to probe the mystery. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14400004345121676069"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Pierre Boulle (20 February 1912 – 30 January 1994) was a French novelist best known for two works, <i>The Bridge over the River Kwai</i> (1952) and <i>Planet of the Apes</i> (1963) that were both made into award-winning films.<br/><br/>Boulle was an engineer serving as a secret agent with the Free French in Singapore, when he was captu</span>
  <span id="freeText14400004345121676069" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Pierre Boulle (20 February 1912 – 30 January 1994) was a French novelist best known for two works, <i>The Bridge over the River Kwai</i> (1952) and <i>Planet of the Apes</i> (1963) that were both made into award-winning films.<br /><br />Boulle was an engineer serving as a secret agent with the Free French in Singapore, when he was captured and subjected to two years' forced labour. He used these experiences in <i>The Bridge over the River Kwai</i>, about the notorious Death Railway, which became an international bestseller. The film by David Lean won many Oscars, and Boulle was credited with writing the screenplay, because its two genuine authors had been blacklisted.<br /><br />His science-fiction novel <i>Planet of the Apes</i>, where intelligent apes gain mastery over humans, was adapted into a series of five award-winning films that spawned magazine versions and popular themed toys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14400004345121676069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
